[?1049h[?1h=FIND(1)                                                                                 General Commands Manual                                                                                FIND(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       find - search for files in a directory hierarchy[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mfind[0m [-H] [-L] [-P] [-D debugopts] [-Olevel] [path...] [expression][m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       This  manual  page  documents the GNU version of [1mfind[0m.  GNU [1mfind[0m searches the directory tree rooted at each given file name by evaluating the given expression from left to right, according to[m
       the rules of precedence (see section OPERATORS), until the outcome is known (the left hand side is false for [4mand[24m operations, true for [4mor[24m), at which point [1mfind[0m moves on to the next file name.[m
[m
       If you are using [1mfind[0m in an environment where security is important (for example if you are using it to search directories that are writable by other users), you  should  read  the  "Security[m
       Considerations" chapter of the findutils documentation, which is called [1mFinding[0m [1mFiles[0m and comes with findutils.   That document also includes a lot more detail and discussion than this manual[m
       page, so you may find it a more useful source of information.[m
[m
[1mOPTIONS[0m[m
       The [1m-H[0m, [1m-L[0m and [1m-P[0m options control the treatment of symbolic links.  Command-line arguments following these are taken to be names of files or directories to be examined, up to the first  argu‚Äê[m
       ment that begins with `-', or the argument `(' or `!'.  That argument and any following arguments are taken to be the expression describing what is to be searched for.  If no paths are given,[m
       the current directory is used.  If no expression is given, the expression [1m-print[0m is used (but you should probably consider using [1m-print0[0m instead, anyway).[m
[m
       This manual page talks about `options' within the expression list.  These options control the behaviour of [1mfind[0m but are specified immediately after  the  last  path  name.   The  five  `real'[m
       options  [1m-H[0m,  [1m-L[0m,  [1m-P[0m,  [1m-D[0m and [1m-O[0m must appear before the first path name, if at all.  A double dash [1m--[0m can also be used to signal that any remaining arguments are not options (though ensuring[m
       that all start points begin with either `./' or `/' is generally safer if you use wildcards in the list of start points).[m
[m
       -P     Never follow symbolic links.  This is the default behaviour.  When [1mfind[0m examines or prints information a file, and the file is a symbolic link, the information used shall be taken from[m
              the properties of the symbolic link itself.[m
[m
       -L     Follow symbolic links.  When [1mfind[0m examines or prints information about files, the information used shall be taken from the properties of the file to which the link points, not from the[m
              link itself (unless it is a broken symbolic link or [1mfind[0m is unable to examine the file to which the link points).  Use of this option implies [1m-noleaf[0m.  If you later use the [1m-P[0m  option,[m
              [1m-noleaf[0m  will  still  be in effect.  If [1m-L[0m is in effect and [1mfind[0m discovers a symbolic link to a subdirectory during its search, the subdirectory pointed to by the symbolic link will be[m
              searched.[m
[m
              When the [1m-L[0m option is in effect, the [1m-type[0m predicate will always match against the type of the file that a symbolic link points to rather than the link itself (unless the symbolic link[m
              is broken).  Using [1m-L[0m causes the [1m-lname[0m and [1m-ilname[0m predicates always to return false.[m
[m
       -H     Do  not  follow  symbolic links, except while processing the command line arguments.  When [1mfind[0m examines or prints information about files, the information used shall be taken from the[m
              properties of the symbolic link itself.   The only exception to this behaviour is when a file specified on the command line is a symbolic link, and the link can be resolved.  For  that[m
              situation,  the  information  used  is  taken from whatever the link points to (that is, the link is followed).  The information about the link itself is used as a fallback if the file[m
              pointed to by the symbolic link cannot be examined.  If [1m-H[0m is in effect and one of the paths specified on the command line is a symbolic link to  a  directory,  the  contents  of  that[m
              directory will be examined (though of course -maxdepth 0 would prevent this).[m
[m
       If  more  than one of [1m-H[0m, [1m-L[0m and [1m-P[0m is specified, each overrides the others; the last one appearing on the command line takes effect.  Since it is the default, the [1m-P[0m option should be consid‚Äê[m
       ered to be in effect unless either [1m-H[0m or [1m-L[0m is specified.[m
[m
       GNU [1mfind[0m frequently stats files during the processing of the command line itself, before any searching has begun.  These options also affect how those arguments are processed.   Specifically,[m
       there  are  a  number  of tests that compare files listed on the command line against a file we are currently considering.  In each case, the file specified on the command line will have been[m
       examined and some of its properties will have been saved.  If the named file is in fact a symbolic link, and the [1m-P[0m option is in effect (or if neither [1m-H[0m nor [1m-L[0m were specified), the  informa‚Äê[m
       tion  used  for  the comparison will be taken from the properties of the symbolic link.  Otherwise, it will be taken from the properties of the file the link points to.  If [1mfind[0m cannot follow[m
       the link (for example because it has insufficient privileges or the link points to a nonexistent file) the properties of the link itself will be used.[m
[m
       When the [1m-H[0m or [1m-L[0m [1moptions[0m [1mare[0m [1min[0m [1meffect,[0m [1many[0m [1msymbolic[0m [1mlinks[0m [1mlisted[0m as the argument of [1m-newer[0m will be dereferenced, and the timestamp will be taken from the file to  which  the  symbolic  link[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 1 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       points.  The same consideration applies to [1m-newerXY[0m, [1m-anewer[0m and [1m-cnewer[0m.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 2 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 5 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       The  [1m-follow[0m  option has a similar effect to [1m-L[0m, though it takes effect at the point where it appears (that is, if [1m-L[0m is not used but [1m-follow[0m is, any symbolic links appearing after [1m-follow[0m on[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 6 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       the command line will be dereferenced, and those before it will not).[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 7 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 8 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       -D debugoptions[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 9 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Print diagnostic information; this can be helpful to diagnose problems with why [1mfind[0m is not doing what you want.  The list of debug options should be comma separated.  Compatibility of[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 10 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              the debug options is not guaranteed between releases of findutils.  For a complete list of valid debug options, see the output of [1mfind[0m [1m-D[0m [1mhelp[0m.  Valid debug options include[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 11 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 12 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              help   Explain the debugging options[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 13 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 14 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              tree   Show the expression tree in its original and optimised form.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 15 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 16 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              stat   Print messages as files are examined with the [1mstat[0m and [1mlstat[0m system calls.  The [1mfind[0m program tries to minimise such calls.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 17 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 18 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              opt    Prints diagnostic information relating to the optimisation of the expression tree; see the -O option.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 19 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 20 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              rates  Prints a summary indicating how often each predicate succeeded or failed.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 21 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 22 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K       -Olevel[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 23 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              Enables  query  optimisation.   The [1mfind[0m program reorders tests to speed up execution while preserving the overall effect; that is, predicates with side effects are not reordered rela‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 24 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              tive to each other.  The optimisations performed at each optimisation level are as follows.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 25 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 26 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              0      Equivalent to optimisation level 1.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 27 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 28 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              1      This is the default optimisation level and corresponds to the traditional behaviour.  Expressions are reordered so that tests based only on the names of files (for example [1m-name[0m[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 29 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                     and [1m-regex[0m) are performed first.[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 30 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 32 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              2      Any  [1m-type[0m or [1m-xtype[0m tests are performed after any tests based only on the names of files, but before any tests that require information from the inode.  On many modern versions[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 33 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                     of Unix, file types are returned by [1mreaddir()[0m and so these predicates are faster to evaluate than predicates which need to stat the file first.  If you use the [1m-fstype[0m [4mFOO[24m pred‚Äê[m
[7m Manual page find(1) line 34 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K                     icate and specify a filsystem type [4mFOO[24m which is not known (that is, present in `/etc/mtab') at the time [1mfind[0m starts, that predicate is equivalent to [1m-false[0m.[m

[7m Manual page find(1) line 36 (press h for help or q to quit)[27m[K[K [KESCESC[KOO[KBB[K              3      At  this  optimisation level, the full cost-based query optimiser is enabled.   -  (hyphen) do not pad the field

[?1049h[?1h=DU(1)                                                                                        User Commands                                                                                       DU(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       du - estimate file space usage[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mdu[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
       [1mdu[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [4m--files0-from=F[24m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Summarize disk usage of each FILE, recursively for directories.[m
[m
       Mandatory arguments to long options are mandatory for short options too.[m
[m
       [1m-0[0m, [1m--null[0m[m
              end each output line with 0 byte rather than newline[m
[m
       [1m-a[0m, [1m--all[0m[m
              write counts for all files, not just directories[m
[m
       [1m--apparent-size[0m[m
              print apparent sizes, rather than disk usage; although the apparent size is usually smaller, it may be larger due to holes in ('sparse') files, internal fragmentation, indirect blocks,[m
              and the like[m
[m
       [1m-B[0m, [1m--block-size[0m=[4mSIZE[24m[m
              scale sizes by SIZE before printing them; e.g., '-BM' prints sizes in units of 1,048,576 bytes; see SIZE format below[m
[m
       [1m-b[0m, [1m--bytes[0m[m
              equivalent to '--apparent-size [1m--block-size[0m=[4m1[24m'[m
[m
       [1m-c[0m, [1m--total[0m[m
              produce a grand total[m
[m
       [1m-D[0m, [1m--dereference-args[0m[m
              dereference only symlinks that are listed on the command line[m
[m
       [1m-d[0m, [1m--max-depth[0m=[4mN[24m[m
              print the total for a directory (or file, with [1m--all[0m) only if it is N or fewer levels below the command line argument;  [1m--max-depth[0m=[4m0[24m is the same as [1m--summarize[0m[m
[m
       [1m--files0-from[0m=[4mF[24m[m
              summarize disk usage of the NUL-terminated file names specified in file F; if F is -, then read names from standard input[m
[m
       [1m-H[0m     equivalent to [1m--dereference-args[0m ([1m-D[0m)[m
[m
       [1m-h[0m, [1m--human-readable[0m[m
              print sizes in human readable format (e.g., 1K 234M 2G)[m
[m
       [1m--inodes[0m[m
              list inode usage information instead of block usage[m
[m
       [1m-k[0m     like [1m--block-size[0m=[4m1K[24m[m
[m

„ÄÄÊàñÔºödu [ÈÄâÈ°π]... --files0-from=F
Summarize disk usage of each FILE, recursively for directories.

Mandatory arguments to long options are mandatory for short options too.
  -0, --null            end each output line with 0 byte rather than newline
  -a, --all             write counts for all files, not just directories
      --apparent-size   print apparent sizes, rather than disk usage; although
                          the apparent size is usually smaller, it may be
                          larger due to holes in ('sparse') files, internal
                          fragmentation, indirect blocks, and the like
  -B, --block-size=SIZE  scale sizes by SIZE before printing them; e.g.,
                           '-BM' prints sizes in units of 1,048,576 bytes;
                           see SIZE format below
  -b, --bytes           equivalent to '--apparent-size --block-size=1'
  -c, --total           produce a grand total
  -D, --dereference-args  dereference only symlinks that are listed on the
                          command line
  -d, --max-depth=N     print the total for a directory (or file, with --all)
                          only if it is N or fewer levels below the command
                          line argument;  --max-depth=0 is the same as
                          --summarize
      --files0-from=F   summarize disk usage of the
                          NUL-terminated file names specified in file F;
                          if F is -, then read names from standard input
  -H                    equivalent to --dereference-args (-D)
  -h, --human-readable  print sizes in human readable format (e.g., 1K 234M 2G)
      --inodes          list inode usage information instead of block usage
  -k                    like --block-size=1K
  -L, --dereference     dereference all symbolic links
  -l, --count-links     count sizes many times if hard linked
  -m                    like --block-size=1M
  -P, --no-dereference  don't follow any symbolic links (this is the default)
  -S, --separate-dirs   for directories do not include size of subdirectories
      --si              like -h, but use powers of 1000 not 1024
  -s, --summarize       display only a total for each argument
  -t, --threshold=SIZE  exclude entries smaller than SIZE if positive,
                          or entries greater than SIZE if negative
      --time            show time of the last modification of any file in the
                          directory, or any of its subdirectories
      --time=WORD       show time as WORD instead of modification time:
                          atime, access, use, ctime or status
      --time-style=STYLE  show times using STYLE, which can be:
                            full-iso, long-iso, iso, or +FORMAT;
                            FORMAT is interpreted like in 'date'
  -X, --exclude-from=FILE  exclude files that match any pattern in FILE
      --exclude=PATTERN    exclude files that match PATTERN
  -x, --one-file-system    skip directories on different file systems
      --help		ÊòæÁ§∫Ê≠§Â∏ÆÂä©‰ø°ÊÅØÂπ∂ÈÄÄÂá∫
      --version		ÊòæÁ§∫ÁâàÊú¨‰ø°ÊÅØÂπ∂ÈÄÄÂá∫

SIZE is an integer and optional unit (example: 10M is 10*1024*1024).  Units
are K, M, G, T, P, E, Z, Y (powers of 1024) or KB, MB, ... (powers of 1000).

[?1049h[?1h=WC(1)                                                                                        User Commands                                                                                       WC(1)[m
[m
[1mNAME[0m[m
       wc - print newline, word, and byte counts for each file[m
[m
[1mSYNOPSIS[0m[m
       [1mwc[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [[4mFILE[24m]...[m
       [1mwc[0m [[4mOPTION[24m]... [4m--files0-from=F[24m[m
[m
[1mDESCRIPTION[0m[m
       Print  newline,  word,  and byte counts for each FILE, and a total line if more than one FILE is specified.  With no FILE, or when FILE is -, read standard input.  A word is a non-zero-length[m
       sequence of characters delimited by white space.  The options below may be used to select which counts are printed, always in the following order: newline, word, character, byte, maximum line[m
       length.[m
[m
       [1m-c[0m, [1m--bytes[0m[m
              print the byte counts[m
[m
       [1m-m[0m, [1m--chars[0m[m
              print the character counts[m
[m
       [1m-l[0m, [1m--lines[0m[m
              print the newline counts[m
[m
       [1m--files0-from[0m=[4mF[24m[m
              read input from the files specified by NUL-terminated names in file F; If F is - then read names from standard input[m
[m
       [1m-L[0m, [1m--max-line-length[0m[m
              print the length of the longest line[m
[m
       [1m-w[0m, [1m--words[0m[m
              print the word counts[m
[m
       [1m--help[0m display this help and exit[m
[m
       [1m--version[0m[m
              output version information and exit[m
[m
       GNU coreutils online help: <http://www.gnu.org/software/coreutils/> Report wc translation bugs to <http://translationproject.org/team/>[m
[m
[1mAUTHOR[0m[m
       Written by Paul Rubin and David MacKenzie.[m
[m
[1mCOPYRIGHT[0m[m
       Copyright ¬© 2013 Free Software Foundation, Inc.  License GPLv3+: GNU GPL version 3 or later <http://gnu.org/licenses/gpl.html>.[m
       This is free software: you are free to change and redistribute it.  There is NO WARRANTY, to the extent permitted by law.[m
[m
[1mSEE[0m [1mALSO[0m[m
       The full documentation for [1mwc[0m is maintained as a Texinfo manual.  If the [1minfo[0m and [1mwc[0m programs are properly installed at your site, the command[m
[m
              [1minfo[0m [1mcoreutils[0m [1m'wc[0m [1minvocation'[0m[m
[m
       should give you access to the complete manual.[m
